English

With the formula “For food thee, for strength thee,”3 he cuts that twig which lies towards the east or north, which has many leaves, many smaller twigs and whose tip is not dried up. With the formula, “You are movers; you are approachers,”4 he drives away calves. Then he impels their mothers with the formula, “May god Savity lead you for the highest deed. O (cows who are) not to be killed, do you swell the share of gods, O strong ones, full of milk, having offspring, free from sickness, from disease. Let He not the thief, the evil-doer have control over you; let Rudra’s dart avoid you.

English

He gazes at the sacrificer with the formula, “Be firm and numerous with this lord of cattle.” With the formula, “Do thou guard the sacrificer’s cattle,” he moves around the twig along the front of the ─Аhavan─лya, brings in by the eastern door and fixes it on the cart standing to the rear of the Garhapatya fire or in the northern half of the (G─Бrhapatya) fire-chamber. This is if the sacrificer is going to offer the S─Бс╣Бn─Бyya.

Then he goes towards the ─Аhavan─лya with the formula, “this wise8 (sickle) has gone towards the sacrificial grass (made by Manu chisled with food). After the Agnihotra has been offered in the evening, the Adhvaryu spreads grassblades towards the north of the G─Бrhapatya and deposits on them four implements, namely, milking pot, purifying darbha-blades and two vessels for boiling S─Бс╣Бn─Бyya-milk. He then sprinkles them with water three times with the formula, “You become purified for the divine rite, for the offering to the gods.28
Then having sat down to the rear of the G─Бrhapatya fire, he draws out burning embers with the fire-stirring stick towards the north with the formula, “You are the heat of M─Бtari┼Ыvan.”29

Catching hold of it, he remains restraining his speech. Then he gazes at the cows which are coming, with the verse, “These cows are coming, yielding sweet milk, having offspring, glorious, multicoloured. English

If there is no cart, he places the wooden sword to the rear of the G─Бrhapatya a pan on the wooden sword and pours grains for the cakes in that pan. He then touches the eastern half of the pan with the formula, “Thou art the yoke; do thou injure him who injures us; do thou injure him whom we injure. Thou belongst to gods, the most firmly joined, the most richly filled, the most agreeable, the best of carriers, the best caller of gods, thou art the oblation-holder that dost not waver; do thou be firm; do thou not waver.”53 Then he gazes at (the grains) to be used for the cakes with the formula, “I gaze at thee with Mitras’ eye; do not be afraid; do not shiver; may I not kill thee.”54 With the formula “(Be thou) wide open to the wind”55 he throws away a grass-blade or beard of corn. Having touched water, having pronounced the Da┼Ыahotr╠е formula56 and having addressed the sacrificer with “I shall pour out obation-material” he pours out grains with the Agnihotra-ladle provided with the strainers.

He places the pestle (into the mortar) with the formula, “Thou art the stone of wood; do thou render agreeable this oblation for gods.”70
He then calls the preparer of oblation three times, “O preparer of oblation, come; O preparer of oblation, come” (and “in order to strike from high”). He strikes at the lower and upper crushing stones with a stone (from high) heavily with the formula, “Proclaim food; proclaim strength, do you make glorious sounds; may we be victorious in contest.”71 Having pounded (with the pestle) and having husked the grains, he places the winnowing basket towards the north with the formula, “thou art grown by rains.”72

рд╡рд┐рд╢реНрд╡рд╛рд╕-рдкреНрд░рд╕реНрддреБрддрд┐рдГ

With the call, “Do you bake (the cake) without burning them.”113 After having heated the wash-water in the pan by means of an ember and having carried forth, he pours it down within the altar in three lines ending westwards with the formula, “Sv─Бh─Б to Ekata, sv─Бh─Б to Dvita, sv─Бh─Б to Trita.”114

English

He carries away (the dust) together with the darbha-blade for the fourth time without reciting any formula.

He does the first tracing of the altar-towards the south with the formula, “May Vasus trace thee with the G─Бyatr─л metre,” towards the west with the formula, “May Rudras trace thee with the Triс╣гс╣нubh metre,” towards the north with the formula тАЬMay ─Аdityas trace thee with the Jagat─л metre.”127 Then he murmurs the Karaс╣Зa formula, тАЬO men, having come, do you prepare this altar occupied by Vasus, Rudras, and ─Аdityas at the height of the heaven, on the navel of the earth so that this sacrificer may not be injured."128 Then he digs out the altar by means of the wooden sword towards the east, with the formula, “On the impulse of god Savitr╠е, wise men perform the rite.”129 He says to the ─Аgn─лdhra, тАЬO Agn─лdh, do you carry away (dust) thrice from here."

He purifies the Prokс╣гaс╣З─л-water with the verse, тАЬMay god Savitr╠е purify you with a flawless strainer with the rays of the bright sun"154 recited in quarters.

He amply covers (the altar) from east to west in three rows (densely) so as not to see through. He keeps back one fire-stick. When he listens to the Hotr╠е uttering the words ─Б juhot─Б duvasyat─Б, he fans the fire three times by means of the Veda. After the S─Бmidhen─л verses have been recited, after having taken up a spoonful from the clarified butter in the Dhruv─Б, having supported (the spoon) with the Veda, he offers an ─Аgh─Бra-libation across with the formula, “For Praj─Бpati, sv─Бh─Б” uttered mentally. Then he gives out a call, тАЬO Agn─лdh, do you cleanse the fires three times each." The ─Аgn─лdhra, having fixed the cord of faggot on the wooden sword, cleanses the enclosing sticks-three times the middle one, three times the southern one and three times the northern one.

He fans the ─Аhavan─лya fire three times with the formula, “O Agni, the winner of wealth, I cleanse for the winning of wealth, for the sake of food, thee who art going to flow wealth, who art going to win wealth, who art the winner of wealth and who art eater of food.”187 In front of Juh┼л and the Upabhr╠еt he holds his palms eastwards with the formula, “Thou art the world, do thou be extended, O Agni the sacrificer, this obeisance to thee.”188 He takes up the Juh┼л with the right hand with the formula, “O Juh┼л, do thou come hither; Agni summons thee for the offering to gods,”189

English

Having cleansed and heated the ladle and having filled it with water, he pours that water outside the enclosing sticks with the verse, “O Agni, do thou not harm in the highest abode the ocean, the hundred-streamed extending in the middle of the region, Aditi giving ghee for men.”205 At this juncture he brings the entire clarified butter from the Upabhr╠еt into the Juh┼л. Having placed the ladles into their places, he cuts up the Pr─Б┼Ыitra of the size of a barley-grain from the northern portion of the southern cake with the verse, “May this oblation less than a barley-grain be cut out at the spot where the sacrifice was hit. May we not disturb the sacrifice. This oblation is pure and well-offered.”206 Having applied clarified butter to it by means of the handle of the spoon and having placed it to the rear of the Praс╣З─лt─Б-waters, he applies water to the handle of the spoon and puts it down.

English

Taking four spoonfuls of clarified butter, he says loudly, “Do you recite the puronuv─Бky─Б” (in low tone) “for wives of gods.” Having caused to announce, he says loudly, “Do you recite the y─Бjy─Б” (in low tone) “for wives of gods.” At the Vaс╣гaс╣н-utterance he makes the offering to wives of gods in the enclosed chamber. Taking four spoonfuls of clarified butter he says loudly, тАЬDo you recite the puronuv─Бky─БтАЭ (in low tone) “for Gr╠еhapati Agni.тАЭ At the Vaс╣гaс╣н-utterance he makes the offering in the eastern half of the northern half beyond the earlier offerings. Having gone beyond in front of the Hotr╠е, he anoints twice the (fore) finger of the Hotr╠е.

English

Having taken up another four spoonfuls and having put the cuttings of faggot on the Anv─Бh─Бryapacana itself and having poured the chaff of grains, he offers the oblation of chaff of grains with the formula, “O Agni, with life unhurt, with not-cool body, guard me this day from the sky, guard me from bondage, guard me from error in sacrifice, guard from evil food, guard from ill deed; render our food poisonless; render our seat comfortably occupiable, sv─Бh─Б.тАЭ224

Having returned by the same route by which he had gone and having handed over the Veda to the Hotr╠е, he unties the girdle round the waist of the sacrificer’s wife with the verse, “I loosen this bond of Varuс╣Зa which Savitr╠е, the kindly, has bound. And with birth-place of the erector, in the place of good action, I make it pleasant for me with my husband.”225 Having put the girdle into her folded hands, he empties a pot filled with water with the verse, “O Agni, I become united with life, and offspring, and with splendour more and more with my husband as wife. May my spirit be united with my body.”226 He cleanses his face with the verse, “The honey which, O Sarasvati, thou hast in water, in the cattle and in the horses, with that honey, O Sarasvati, do thou strong, besmear my mouth.”227 He pours down the water. “Having rendered the form of Avabhr╠еtha he gets up.” So says the Br─Бhmaс╣Зa.228

Then (the Adhvaryu) causes her (the sacrificer’s wife) to sip water across the strainers with the verse, “The plants are full of sap; the sap of creepers is full of sap. O Indu, do thou unite me with that sap which is of the sap of water.”229

Then he makes her put a fire-stick on the G─Бrhapatya with the formula, “O Agni, lord of vows, I have observed the vow; I have been capable of it; it has flourished for me, sv─Бh─Б. O V─Бyu, lord of vows, O ─Аditya, lord of vows; O lord of the vows, I have observed the vow; I have been capable of it; it has flourished for me, sv─Бh─Б.тАЭ Then he makes her leave by the route by which she had entered.

Moving to the east, he swells the Dhruva with the verse, “May the Dhruva swell with ghee in this sacrifice and in each sacrifice for the purpose of the fruits, the bosom of S┼лrya (in the lap of Aditi), the earth with wide streams.230 Taking up clarified butter from the vessel of clarified butter by means of the spoon, he makes the expiation-offerings: “The sacrifice goes on compensating the limits-the announcing, overannouncing, Vaс╣гaс╣н-utterance, over-reciting, overacting, deficient acting. May the offering made to the accompaniment of sv─Бh─Б-utterance reach the gods, sv─Бh─Б.” He makes the offerings promoting the sacrifice: “To thou whom sacrifice has been offered, sv─Бh─Б; to the divinities to whom offerings have not been made at the Vaс╣гaс╣н-utterance, sv─Бh─Б; the remedy for the ill sacrifice, sv─Бh─Б; to Niс╣гkr╠еti sv─Бh─Б; to Daur─Бrdhi sv─Бh─Б; to the divine bodies sv─Бh─Б; to R╠еddhi, sv─Бh─Б; to Samr╠еddhi, sv─Бh─Б; to all round Samr╠еddhi sv─Бh├в; bh┼лс╕е sv─Бh─Б; bhuvaс╕е sv─Бh─Б; suvaс╕е sv─Бh─Б, bh┼лr bhuvaс╕е suvaс╕е sv─Бh─Б. Do thou O Varuс╣Зa, harken my invocation, do favour to me today. Seeking thy favour, I implore thee. Praying to thee with the divine song, I come to thee. The sacrificer seeks that (favour of thine) through oblations. Without getting angry, O Varuс╣Зa, do thou know of this (divine song). Praised widely, do thou not steal away our life-Do thou O Agni, the wise, pacify the anger of god Varuс╣Зa. The best of sacrificers, the best messenger of god, the brilliant, do thou remove all evil spirits from us-Do thou O Agni, be nearest to us, closest to help, at the dawning of the dawn, bestowing wealth on us, do thou appease Varuс╣Зa through sacrifice for us; show thy mercy and be ready to hear our call. Thou art swift Agni. Being swift, thou art placed in the mind (as a messenger to gods); being swift, thou carriest the oblation, being swift, give us remedy. Thou art swift, O Agni, and free from censure. Really thou art swift, supported by swift, thou carriest oblation swiftly, swift do thou grant us remedy, Sv─Бh─Б. With the oblation I appease what we have passed over in this rite in the form of Mantra or action. May the gods be satiated and compensate through clarified butter. What I have done in excess in this rite,
what I have done less here, may Sviс╣гс╣нakr╠еt Agni, knowing it, do it well offered for me-To Sviс╣гс╣нakr╠еt Agni, the well offerer of oblations, the fulfiller of desires, Sv─Бh─Б-O Praj─Бpati, none else than thee surrounded all those creations. May we obtain those objects desiring which we offer thee. May we be lords of wealth, sv─Бh─Б.”231

рдореВрд▓рдореН

рдЕрде рдмрд░реНрд╣рд┐рд╖реЛ рдзрд╛рддреВрдирд╛рдБрд╕рдореНрдкреНрд░рд▓реБрдкреНрдп рдзреНрд░реБрд╡рд╛рдпрд╛рдБрд╕рдордирдХреНрддрд┐ рд╕рдордЩреНрдХреНрддрд╛рдВ рдмрд░реНрд╣рд┐рд░реНрд╣рд╡рд┐рд╖рд╛ рдШреГрддреЗрди рд╕рдорд╛рджрд┐рддреНрдпреИрд░реНрд╡рд╕реБрднрд┐рдГ рд╕рдВ рдорд░реБрджреНрднрд┐рдГ ред рд╕рдорд┐рдиреНрджреНрд░реЗ рдг рд╡рд┐рд╢реНрд╡реЗрднрд┐рд░реНрджреЗрд╡реЗрднрд┐рд░рдЩреНрдХреНрддрд╛рдорд┐рддреНрдпрдереИрдирджрд╛рд╣рд╡рдиреАрдпреЗрд╜рдиреБрдкреНрд░рд╣рд░рддрд┐ рджрд┐рд╡реНрдпрдВ рдирднреЛ рдЧрдЪреНрдЫрддреБ рдпрддреНрд╕реНрд╡рд╛рд╣реЗрддреНрдпрдереЛрдкреЛрддреНрдерд╛рдп рджрдХреНрд╖рд┐рдгреЗрди рдкрджрд╛ рд╡реЗрджрд┐рдорд╡рдХреНрд░рдореНрдп рдзреНрд░реБрд╡рдпрд╛ рд╕рдорд┐рд╖реНрдЯрдпрдЬреБрд░реНрдЬреБрд╣реЛрддрд┐ рджреЗрд╡рд╛ рдЧрд╛рддреБрд╡рд┐рджреЛ рдЧрд╛рддреБрдВ рд╡рд┐рддреНрддреНрд╡рд╛ рдЧрд╛рддреБрдорд┐рдд рдордирд╕рд╕реНрдкрдд рдЗрдордВ рдиреЛ рджреЗрд╡ рджреЗрд╡реЗрд╖реБ рдпрдЬреНрдЮрдБрд╕реНрд╡рд╛рд╣рд╛ рд╡рд╛рдЪрд┐ рд╕реНрд╡рд╛рд╣рд╛ рд╡рд╛рддреЗ рдзрд╛рдГ рд╕реНрд╡рд╛рд╣реЗрддреНрдпреБрджреВрд╣рддрд┐ рд╕реНрд░реБрдЪрдВ рдирд┐рдирдпрддрд┐ рдкреНрд░рдгреАрддрд╛ рдЙрдкреЛрддреНрдерд╛рдп рдпрдЬрдорд╛рдиреЛ рджрдХреНрд╖рд┐рдгреЗрди рдкрджрд╛ рд╡рд┐рд╖реНрдгреБрдХреНрд░рдорд╛рдиреНрдХреНрд░рдорддреЗ

English

Having snatched a few bundles of sacrificial grass, he dips them into the Dhruva with the verse, “May the sacrificial grass be smeared with the oblation of clarified butter together with ─Аdityas, Vasus, Maruts, Indra and Vi┼Ыve Devas. May it go to the heaven, sv─Бh─Б.тАЭ232 Having stood up, and having crossed the altar with the right leg, he makes the Samiс╣гс╣нayajus offering by means of the Dhruva with the formula, “O gods, knowers of path, having known the path, do you follow the path. O god, lord of mind, carry on this our sacrifice unto gods, sv─Бh─Б, sv─Бh─Б unto the speech; place it unto wind, sv─Бh─Б.”233 He lifts up the ladle, pours down the Praс╣З─лt─Б-water (into the altar). Having stood up, the sacrificer takes Viс╣гс╣Зu-strides.”234

рд╡рд┐рд╢реНрд╡рд╛рд╕-рдкреНрд░рд╕реНрддреБрддрд┐рдГ

рд╕рдиреНрддрд┐рд╖реНрдардд рдЖрдорд╛рд╡рд╛рд╕реНрдпрдВ рд╡рд╛ рдкреМрд░реНрдгрдорд╛рд╕реНрдпрдВ рд╡рд╛ рд╣рд╡рд┐рдГ реирез

рдореВрд▓рдореН

рд╕рдиреНрддрд┐рд╖реНрдардд рдЖрдорд╛рд╡рд╛рд╕реНрдпрдВ рд╡рд╛ рдкреМрд░реНрдгрдорд╛рд╕реНрдпрдВ рд╡рд╛ рд╣рд╡рд┐рдГ реирез

English

The offering pertaining to the new-moon or full-moon comes to an end.
